## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate modeled as an ODE in time t and population size P. Classical population-dynamics models express dP_dt as P times a per-capita rate that depends on density (P) and/or environmental forcing (t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Affine rate with immigration/emigration: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (net constant influx/outflux added to proportional growth)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (self-limitation via negative quadratic term when c1 < 0)
- Cubic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (richer density effects, including multiple equilibria)
- Gompertz-type growth (log-density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - log(P)) (growth slows roughly linearly with log population size)
- Theta-logistic (generalized crowding exponent): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (crowding strength controlled by exponent c2)
- Richards (generalized logistic family without logistic closed-form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)**c3 (flexible sigmoid approach to equilibrium)
- Allee effect (depensation) with carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P - 1) (reduced growth at low P; potential extinction threshold)
- Proportional harvesting (constant effort): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (harvest/mortality proportional to population size)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (fixed removal independent of P over modeled range)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment affecting per-capita growth)
- Seasonally forced density dependence: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t + c3)) * P * (1 - c4 * P) (periodic r(t) combined with crowding)
- Time-varying carrying capacity (trend): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t)) (effective capacity changes exponentially with time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope Γ¶Ê Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects Γ¶Ê Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay Γ¶Ê Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior Γ¶Ê Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects Γ¶Ê Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dP_dt is approximately proportional to P across all samples, a density-independent per-capita rate is indicated: dP_dt Γëê P * r(t) or dP_dt Γëê c * P.
- Negative curvature in dP_dt vs P (growth increasing then decreasing) suggests self-limitation, typically captured by adding a negative P**2 term or a factor (1 - c*P).
- Multiple equilibria (dP_dt crossing zero more than once as P varies) is a hallmark of higher-order density dependence or Allee effects, often requiring cubic-like structure in P.
- If per-capita growth (dP_dt / P) decreases roughly linearly with log(P), Gompertz-type structure dP_dt ΓêÙ P*(const - log(P)) is favored.
- Sharper-than-quadratic decline at high P (very strong crowding) often points to generalized exponents: terms like (c*P)**c2 with c2 > 1.
- A positive growth-to-decline transition that shifts over time suggests explicit time dependence in r(t) and/or K(t), e.g., multiplicative exp(c*t) or periodic sin/cos forcing.
- Observed oscillations in dP_dt at fixed P (or in residuals after removing P-effects) indicate seasonal/environmental forcing: r(t) = c0 + c1*sin(c2*t + c3).
- A near-constant downward offset in dP_dt (independent of P) suggests constant-yield removal, whereas a downward term proportional to P suggests proportional mortality/harvesting.

Combined:
```
GT = 0.22848*P - 0.002807*P┬▓ - 0.11424*P*exp(-0.08368*P) + 0.11424*P*exp(-0.08368*t)
```

So the GT has these basis function components:
1. **P** (linear in P)
2. **P┬▓** (quadratic in P)
3. **P┬╖exp(-╬▒P)** (P times exponential in P)
4. **P┬╖exp(-╬▓t)** (P times exponential in t)

The key distinctive features are:
- **P┬╖exp(-0.08368*P)**: This is a critical nonlinear term mixing P with exp(P)
- **P┬╖exp(-0.08368*t)**: This mixes P with exp(t)

Now let me check each candidate for the presence of these basis functions.

### Critical basis functions needed:
- `P*exp(c*P)` ΓÇË very few candidates have this
- `P*exp(c*t)` ΓÇË need this too

Let me scan candidates for `P*exp(...)` terms:

Most candidates use `log(P*c + 1)`, `P**c`, `tanh`, `t/sqrt(P+c)`, `exp(c*t)` (without P multiplier), etc.

**The term P┬╖exp(-╬▒P) is crucial.** Let me check which candidates could produce this:

- `log(P*c + 1)` Γëê This is a logarithm, not equivalent to P┬╖exp(cP)
- `P**c` ΓÇË power law, not equivalent
- `exp(c*sin(...))` ΓÇË trigonometric, not equivalent

**The term P┬╖exp(-╬▓t) is also crucial.** This requires a product of P and exp(t). Let me check:

- `exp(c*t)` alone (without P factor) cannot match `P*exp(c*t)` for all P
- `P*c*t` is linear in t, not exponential
- `tanh(c*t+c)` is not exp
- `P*tanh(c*t+c)` ΓÇË tanh is not exp

None of the candidates appear to have both `P*exp(c*P)` and `P*exp(c*t)` terms.

Let me verify more carefully. The GT requires `P*exp(c*t)` ΓÇË a term that is the product of P and an exponential in t. Looking at all candidates:

- Candidates with `exp(c*t)`: Many have this but WITHOUT a P multiplier
- Candidates with `P*tanh(c*t+c)`: tanh Γë¦ exp

For `P*exp(c*P)`: No candidate has exp(c*P) multiplied by P. Candidate 33 has `exp(P*c4)` but not multiplied by P.

Since the GT fundamentally requires `P*exp(-╬▒P)` (a term that cannot be replicated by polynomials, logs, or other basis functions available in the candidates) AND `P*exp(-╬▓t)` (which requires P multiplied by exp(t)), none of the candidates can match.

After careful analysis of all 50 candidates, none contain the necessary `P*exp(c*P)` basis function, and none have `P*exp(c*t)` (product of P with exponential in t). These are linearly independent from all basis functions present in the candidates.

Candidate 1-50 verdict: [NO MATCH] for all.
